    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer8905712558068280338">Gibt es in einer vom Alltag besetzten Wirklichkeit einen besser geschützten Raum für gelebte Sehnsüchte als den virtuellen?<br/><br/>Bei Leo Leike landen irrtümlich E-Mails einer ihm unbekannten Emmi Rothner. Aus Höflichkeit antwortet er ihr. Und weil sich Emmi von ihm angezogen fühlt, schreibt sie zurück.<br/><br/>Bald gibt Leo zu: »Ich interessiere mich wahnsinnig für Sie, liebe Emmi! Ich w</span>
  <span id="freeText8905712558068280338" style="display:none">Gibt es in einer vom Alltag besetzten Wirklichkeit einen besser geschützten Raum für gelebte Sehnsüchte als den virtuellen?<br /><br />Bei Leo Leike landen irrtümlich E-Mails einer ihm unbekannten Emmi Rothner. Aus Höflichkeit antwortet er ihr. Und weil sich Emmi von ihm angezogen fühlt, schreibt sie zurück.<br /><br />Bald gibt Leo zu: »Ich interessiere mich wahnsinnig für Sie, liebe Emmi! Ich weiß aber auch, wie absurd dieses Interesse ist.« Und wenig später gesteht Emmi: »Es sind Ihre Zeilen und meine Reime darauf: die ergeben so in etwa einen Mann, wie ich mir plötzlich vorstelle, dass es sein kann, dass es so jemanden wirklich gibt.«<br /><br />Es scheint nur noch eine Frage der Zeit zu sein, wann es zum ersten persönlichen Treffen kommt, aber diese Frage wühlt beide so sehr auf, dass sie die Antwort lieber noch eine Weile hinauszögern. Außerdem ist Emmi glücklich verheiratet. Und Leo verdaut gerade eine gescheiterte Beziehung.<br /><br />Und überhaupt: Werden die gesendeten, empfangenen und gespeicherten Liebesgefühle einer Begegnung standhalten? Und was, wenn ja?<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8905712558068280338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This book is about internet pals. It begins by chance. Leo receives emails in error from an unknown woman called Emmi. They met each other on the virt<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This book is about internet pals. It begins by chance. Leo receives emails in error from an unknown woman called Emmi. They met each other on the virtual world and are trying to make it true to pass to the real world. This book is translated to farsi entitled as “مفید در برابر باد شمالی”. I gave mine to Maryam 1 month ago. You can read it just by going to her room and find it. :D<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer931705356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2596742640150654874"><b>*****<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629275i/9576684.jpg' width='30' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg' width='30' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg' width='30' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg' width='30' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg' width='30' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg' width='30' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> *****</b><br/><b> ONE SITTING READ RIGHT HERE! ALL NIGHTER! MUST READ! </b><br/><i>Re-read Oct, 22, 2014. Still ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<b> 5 STARS</b> ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️</i><br/><br/>~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~<br/><br/>I don't know where to start to explain you the whirlwind of emotions I experienced last night reading Love Virtually.<br/>But let's rectify something right now... <br/>Who decided to just change the original title of this book? It was called in German : "Gut Gegen Nordwind : <b>Good Against North Wind"</b> And this makes so much more sense!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399634006ra/9577103.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A little </span>
  <span id="freeText2596742640150654874" style="display:none"><b>*****<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629275i/9576684.jpg" width="30" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="30" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="30" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="30" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="30" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="30" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> *****</b><br><b> ONE SITTING READ RIGHT HERE! ALL NIGHTER! MUST READ! </b><br><i>Re-read Oct, 22, 2014. Still ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<b> 5 STARS</b> ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️</i><br><br>~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~<br><br>I don't know where to start to explain you the whirlwind of emotions I experienced last night reading Love Virtually.<br>But let's rectify something right now... <br>Who decided to just change the original title of this book? It was called in German : "Gut Gegen Nordwind : <b>Good Against North Wind"</b> And this makes so much more sense!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399634006ra/9577103.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A little while ago I asked for a book recommendation here on Goodreads, I wanted to know if there was possibly a good book out there with a very specific theme : long distance romance, email or chat correspondence.<br>A Goodread user answered me : <br><br><b>
  <i>"Are you kidding? There's no romance in email, txt, or 'im chat'. Anyone who would even try to write a 'romance' with those elements would be a laughable author, at best. Try this (A. S. Bratt "Possession"), instead. Stay authentic! "</i>
</b><br><br>I obviously was not "kidding" at all. I met the father of my son 14 years ago this very same way.<br>And let me tell you it is very authentic, it was very romantic, we wrote to each other for 3 years, long emails, letters and phone calls. Romanticism can perfectly lives within virtual electronic ways, rest assured.<br>Is Daniel Glattauer a "laughable" author? Absolutely not! He is a genius.<br><br>~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~<br><br>It all started with Emmi, trying to unsubscribe from a magazine with an email which lands by a fortunate mistake in Leo's email box.<br><b>
  <blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> Dear Sir/Madam at "LIKE" magazine,<br>Are you deliberately ignoring my attempts to cancel my subscription? If you're trying to offload more copies of your rag which, let's face it, is gradually going down the drain, I regret to inform you that I'm not going to pay another cent!<br>Best Wishes,<br>E. Rothner</blockquote>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399633164ra/9576963.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It didn't take me long to be hooked, the third email from Emmi's just set the tone of what would be one of the most brilliant and clever dialogues I have ever read between two people. It was just like reading over Emmi and Leo' shoulders, witnessing their mutual discovery of each other. <br><br>Leo had me with his first one... I quickly fell in love with his character. <br><b>
  <blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">You've sent your message to the wrong address. This is a private one : woerter@leike.com.<br>You want woerter@like.com. You're the third person who's sent me an email trying to cancel their subscription. It must be really a shocking magazine. </blockquote>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382362359ra/5847625.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They both pretty quickly develop feelings toward each other without really crossing a virtual line, Emmi is a <b>"happily married"</b> woman after all...<br><b>
  <blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Emmi, you can't stop talking about sex. It's pathological!</blockquote>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384914253ra/7025932.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But that doesn't stop her staking claim of her virtual soulmate... She just can't stop herself, it was really comical AND sad considering the situation...<br><b>
  <blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">I'm sorry to say that yes, IT DOES MATTER TO ME WHEN, HOW, WITH, WHOM AND HOW OFTEN YOU HAVE SEX! If I am indeed somebody's chosen "second voice" then I should also have the right to judge wether it's appropriate when, how, with, whom and how often that person has sex.</blockquote>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399633661ra/9577040.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The whole book is written in email format, no narration at all. I just completely overlooked the fact that no descriptions to their surroundings where given, focusing on their exchange, waiting for one of them to feed me crumbs about their lives. Daniel Glattauer just made it work! I couldn't put this book down!<br><b>
  <blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">She - this Emmi with size 37 shoes - is beginning to interest me more than befits the nature of our correspondence. </blockquote>
</b><br>I still don't know where I am going with this review, weighting the pros and cons to tell you what is going to happen, or let you enjoy the discovery of their corresponding.<br>I just told some friends I would never recommend this book to someone I care about, just to spare them the trouble of having their heart ripped open.<br>If you know me, you should know by now that I hate giving out what is happening in a book unless you read it.<br>I love to experience every little details personally, which is why I often overlook a blurb and try not to read reviews beforehand.<br><b>
  <blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">...Has it occurred to you that we know absolutely nothing about each other? We're creating virtual character, piecing together identikit fantasies of each other... We're toying with and endlessly provoking each other's curiosity by refusing point-blank to satisfy it... Each of us is trying desperately to build up an accurate picture of the other. And by the same time we're being meticulous in not giving away anything fundamental about ourselves. </blockquote>
</b><br>I think you have here an answer to the above, I would HIGHLY recommend EVERYONE to read this book.<br> <b>
  <blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Yes, by all means feel free to write to me! Type away all your frustration with men, from the depths of your soul. Unleash all your self-righteousness, cynicism and gloating. If you feel better afterwards, my inbox has done its job. If you don't, then just treat yourself (or your mother) to another "LIKE" subscription and unsubscribe from "Leike" . </blockquote>
</b><br><br>Love Virtually left me in a hot mess of feelings, it's one of the best romance book I have ever read.<br>Why? Maybe because I have a <b>story</b> with corresponding by email to some stranger that you can't live without. Yes, I met my Leo in very similar circumstances. My own virtual soulmate.<br>I invested myself a tad too much in their story, but the author did not exactly left me a choice here. You cannot NOT wish for Emmi and Leo an happy ending. I was mentally screaming for them to meet and declare their love. <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Or I am the most horrible person in the world, because I truly wanted for Emmi and Leo to have their HEA, in spite of her <b>"Happy Marriage".</b>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399633164ra/9576964.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399629113i/9576653.jpg" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> It's three o'clock in the morning. Is the north wind blowing?<br>Goodnight. </blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399634169ra/9577131.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399633164ra/9576965.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~≈~<br><br><b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20325263-every-seventh-wave" rel="nofollow noopener"> A SEQUEL</a> IS AVAILABLE, <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Every-Seventh-Wave-Daniel-Glattauer-ebook/dp/B00D5AMSO8/ref=pd_sim_sbs_kstore_1?ie=UTF8&amp;refRID=1NQ2XVHV6D631X7MT2R3" rel="nofollow noopener"> HERE</a> at Amazon</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1665646423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1665646423" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1665646423?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857050953" href="/book/show/12640615-love-virtually">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=light-fiction">light-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=4stars">4stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2016">read2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1665646423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8985812172432717437"><b>HALLELUJAH</b> for this little book!!! <b>*happy wiggle*</b><br/>I <i>needed</i> something to lift me out of my life, out of my head... Just something to make me forget the world for a while and this little book waved hello at me with its friendly looking cover and <b>IMMEDIATE</b> hook!!! <br/>From the first page I was <b>gripped</b>.<br/>It was <b>snappy. </b><br/>It felt <b>fresh</b>!<br/>In fact it made me want to keep reading and reading and reading, and turning those pages as quickly as my grubby little fingers could manage!!! <br/><br/><br/>The story is told completely in </span>
  <span id="freeText8985812172432717437" style="display:none"><b>HALLELUJAH</b> for this little book!!! <b>*happy wiggle*</b><br />I <i>needed</i> something to lift me out of my life, out of my head... Just something to make me forget the world for a while and this little book waved hello at me with its friendly looking cover and <b>IMMEDIATE</b> hook!!! <br />From the first page I was <b>gripped</b>.<br />It was <b>snappy. </b><br />It felt <b>fresh</b>!<br />In fact it made me want to keep reading and reading and reading, and turning those pages as quickly as my grubby little fingers could manage!!! <br /><br /><br />The story is told completely in email format between the two main characters. While attempting to unsubscribe from a magazine Emmi accidentally mails the wrong email address and thus begins a rather curious and flirty email correspondence with Leo. The two characters open up to each other and begin to share their thoughts, and even though a romantic relationship could never or indeed should never happen for these two... Well you can guess what begins to unfurl!!!<br /><br /><br />I <b>loved</b> the premise of this book. Imagine getting to know someone through their words alone. No face to distract, no knowledge of their backgrounds, not even the sound of their voice... Nothing but the innermost workings of their mind typed into an email. Despite the lack of physical contact it's a very intimate form of connection between two human beings. And yet what was interesting was that even though we were privy to the inner thoughts of these two main characters we never fully got to know their whole selves. Because the characters were able to pick and choose what part of themselves they shared with the other person, and therefore with the reader. So in a way it's kinda like all of us here on Goodreads: choosing what we do and do not share about our own lives!!! <br /><br /><br />And so was all of this story truly believable??? <br />Well not really... I mean it did quickly get a bit far-fetched especially if you are to believe that these are intelligent, regular people. The characters were a little identikit; she was pretty much your typical cute and quirky female lead, and he was the self-deprecating yet well educated male... <br />But you know what? I didn't have a problem with that. Because it's a rom-com! A good, fun book. <br />There are certain things that I both expect and want from this type of book and this delivered on all of those fronts. And what does make this rom-com standout from others is that it doesn't completely lose itself to being overly saccharine or laden with schmaltz. And the two lead characters weren't always likeable and acted quite selfishly at times which gave this rom-com a slightly edgier tone. <br />Is it predictable??<br />Well yeah, I kinda thought so. But I did reeeeeally like the ending!!! It's the ending I was gunning for. And for good measure, there's a sequel! Yaaaaaaayyyyy!!!! One which I can't wait to get my hands on. I've already been on to my library's website and arranged an inter-library reservation!!! That's a good sign right there <b>*happy grinning*</b><br /><br />So if you're looking for an easy, light read yet something that will hold your attention maybe think about reading this. <br /><br /><br /><b>three and a half stars</b> rounded up to four <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i><br />“Has it occurred to you that we know absolutely nothing about each other? <br />We’re creating virtual characters, piecing together fantasies of each other. We’re asking questions that are never answered, and that’s part of the charm. We’re toying with and endlessly provoking each other’s curiosity by refusing point-blank to satisfy it. <br />We’re trying to read between the lines, and soon I expect we’ll be trying to read between the letters. Each of us is trying desperately to build up an accurate picture of the other. <br />And at the same time we’re being meticulous in not giving away anything fundamental about ourselves. What does “anything fundamental” mean – it means betraying nothing at all; we’ve yet to say anything about our lives, about our everyday existences, about the things that might be important to us.<br />We’re communicating in a vacuum. ...<br />There are no people around us. <br />We don’t inhabit anywhere. <br />We don’t have ages. <br />We don’t have faces. <br />We make no distinction between day and night. We don’t live in any particular time. All we’ve got is our computer screens – for our eyes only – and we share a hobby: we’re both interested in a complete stranger.”</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="8985812172432717437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13925000110547418759">Gut gegen Nordwind = Love Virtually, Daniel Glattauer<br/>Love Virtually is a novel by the Austrian writer Daniel Glattauer. It begins by chance: Leo receives emails in error from an unknown woman called Emmi. Being polite he replies, and Emmi writes back. A few brief exchanges are all it takes to spark a mutual interest in each other, and soon Emmi and Leo are sharing their innermost secrets and longings. Will their feelings for each other survive the test of a real-life encounter? And if so, what t</span>
  <span id="freeText13925000110547418759" style="display:none">Gut gegen Nordwind = Love Virtually, Daniel Glattauer<br />Love Virtually is a novel by the Austrian writer Daniel Glattauer. It begins by chance: Leo receives emails in error from an unknown woman called Emmi. Being polite he replies, and Emmi writes back. A few brief exchanges are all it takes to spark a mutual interest in each other, and soon Emmi and Leo are sharing their innermost secrets and longings. Will their feelings for each other survive the test of a real-life encounter? And if so, what then? Love Virtually is a funny, fast-paced and absorbing experience, with plenty of twists and turns, about a love affair conducted by email.<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و دوم ماه جولای سال 2011 میلادی<br />عنوان: مقابله با باد شمال؛ نویسنده: دانیل گلاتاثور؛ مترجم: مهشید میرمعزی؛ تهران، تندیس، 1389، در 279 ص؛ شابک: 9786001820069؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان انریشی - سده 21 م<br />عنوان: مفید در برابر باد شمالی؛ نویسنده: دانیل گلاتاثور؛ مترجم: شهلا پیام؛ تهران، ققنوس، 1391؛ در 247 ص؛ شابک: 9789643119669؛ چاپ دوم 1394؛ چاپ سوم 1396؛ <br />پیامکی به یک نشانی اشتباه میرسد، کتاب «مفید در برابر باد شمالی» درست با چنین رخدادی آغاز می‌شود، با ایمیلی که تنها با وارد کردن حرفی اضافه در نشانی، سر از مکان و سیستمی دیگر درمی‌آورد. پیامیکه برای پایان دادن به اشتراک یک مجله بوده، سرآغاز داستانی پر شور می‌شود، که تا آخرین واژه خوانشگر را به دنبال خود می‌کشاند، و خوانشگر در تب و تابی برای یافتن پاسخ، به این دو پرسش که: «در انتها چه می‌شود؟» و «آیا یکدیگر را می‌بینند؟» ایجاد می‌کند. چکیده: داستان از ایمیلی ناخواسته آغاز می‌شود، گام بعدی با پاسخی از روی ادب برداشته می‌شود، و سپس داستانی شورانگیز پا می‌گیرد. «امی روتنر»، ایمیلی از سر خشم به یکی از مجلات ارسال می‌کند، اما برای تنها یک حرف اضافه، این ایمیل، به دست «لئو لایکه» می‌رسد، و از همینجاست که داستان آغاز می‌شود. «امی» یا «اما»، زنی متاهل است، که در کنار همسر و دو فرزند خوانده ی خود، زندگی شیرینی دارد. تنها جای خالی در زندگی او، هیجان و راز و رمز است. راز و رمزی که نگارگری با «لئو لایکه»، روانشناسی رنجور، که به تازگی رابطه ی عاشقانه اش شکست خورده، و آن را پشت سر انداخته، در اختیارش قرار می‌دهد. آن دو شخصیت‌هایی خیالی، از روی نوشته‌ ها از آن دیگری در ذهن خود برساخته‌ اند. شخصیت هایی که هیچ ایرادی نداشته، و در برخی موارد، از شخصیت واقعی آن‌ها پیشی بگرفته است. این مشخصه آنجای بیشتر نمایان می‌شود، که این دو، از دیدار یکدیگر هراس دارند. «امی» که در زندگی خود، کوچکترین کمبودی ندارد، تنها ترسش که در اوراق این کتاب قابل لمس است، جذاب نبودن «لئو» ست. این نشان می‌دهد که «لئو»، برای او تصویری برساخته، و پرداخته، که شاید کوچکترین نارسایی در برابر آن تصویر، همه چیز را به هم بریزد. و نشان از این دارد، که نیاز «امی» به او، تنها در حد همان رمز و راز است، و آنگاه که این راز گفته شود، او دیگر نیازی به «لئو»، در زندگی خویش نخواهد داشت. همانگونه که داستان پیش می‌رود، بیش از پیش به دیده می‌نشیند، که با وجود حسی که شکل گرفته، «امی» جریان را به میدان بازی‌ برای خویش بدل کرده است. او هماره قدم نخست را برداشته، و آنگاه که «لئو» از متاهل بودنش باخبر شد، باز هم به عاشق و گرفتار کردن او، اصرار ورزید. در هر روی داستان، شاید به چشم بسیاری، چندان جذاب نیاید، اما بی‌شک خیال انگیز، و برای خوانشگر نوستالژیک است. نقل از متن: «آدم نباید هیچوقت درباره‌ ی از دست دادن فکر کند. حتی با فکر کردن درباره‌ ی آن هم چیزی را از دست می‌دهد.»؛ پایان نقل. ا. شربیانی</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88753519" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2719191-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252501222p2/2719191.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88753519?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/2719191-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2719191-julia?shelf=disliked">disliked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2719191-julia?shelf=austrian">austrian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88753519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11118760354110120198">I was really intrigued by the idea of this book: a modern epistolary novel written only in e-mails, exchanged between a man recovering from a year-long relationship and a - happily? - married woman who know each other only in the virtual world. A modern topic, with all those internet dating sites and with platforms where people form relationships with others based merely on internet profiles. Besides, Daniel Glattauer has been highly acclaimed by the Spiegel magazine and has written columns for </span>
  <span id="freeText11118760354110120198" style="display:none">I was really intrigued by the idea of this book: a modern epistolary novel written only in e-mails, exchanged between a man recovering from a year-long relationship and a - happily? - married woman who know each other only in the virtual world. A modern topic, with all those internet dating sites and with platforms where people form relationships with others based merely on internet profiles. Besides, Daniel Glattauer has been highly acclaimed by the Spiegel magazine and has written columns for my favourite newspaper, the Standard, which was a recommendation of its own for me.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I intensely disliked the characters - seudointellectual, whiny, over-sensitive - the kind of people who claim to write an e-mail in half a minute while the style of the epistle is convuluted and artificially selected and in no way natural or fresh. <br /><br />In favour of the book: it's an extremely fast read, and it kept me mildly interested in the outcome until the slightly surprising end. <br />So one star for the initial idea, and another one - though not a very bright one - for the construction of this ménage-à-trois. <br /><br />Sorry to those i had recommended this too, i was eager to share some contemporary austrian fiction, but i can't wholeheartedly stick to this....<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_157604040" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157604040" />
    <a title="Tammy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3912806-tammy"><img alt="Tammy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442146785p2/3912806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157604040?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammy" href="/user/show/3912806-tammy">Tammy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781906694975" href="/book/show/8928842-love-virtually">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3912806-tammy?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3912806-tammy?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3912806-tammy?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157604040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3843257652681477733"><i>A modern, witty, comedy-of-errors look at just what happens when two people connect through a series of accidental email exchanges.</i><br/><br/><b>Favourite quote from the book:</b> "Write to me Emmi. Writing is like Kissing, but without lips. Writing is kissing with the mind."<br/><br/>It starts in an unexpected, but not completely uncommon manner.<br/><br/>Emmi, a happily married woman, sends a few e-mails to a subscription service with the intent of unsubscribing to a magazine.<br/><br/>By chance, these e-mails inadvertently somehow always m</span>
  <span id="freeText3843257652681477733" style="display:none"><i>A modern, witty, comedy-of-errors look at just what happens when two people connect through a series of accidental email exchanges.</i><br /><br /><b>Favourite quote from the book:</b> "Write to me Emmi. Writing is like Kissing, but without lips. Writing is kissing with the mind."<br /><br />It starts in an unexpected, but not completely uncommon manner.<br /><br />Emmi, a happily married woman, sends a few e-mails to a subscription service with the intent of unsubscribing to a magazine.<br /><br />By chance, these e-mails inadvertently somehow always manage to end up landing in Leo Leike's inbox.<br /><br />And thus begins a daily exchange of conversation filled with witticisms, simmering romantic tension and the sharing of inner most longings between two people who are, in essence, virtual strangers to one another.<br /><br />As with most people who meet online, the inevitable subject of meeting each other outside the virtual realm crops up. Will they meet? And if they do, what happens when the reality isn't as grand as the web-spun fantasy?<br /><br />Is Emmi really prepared to risk her marriage? And what if Leo can't reconcile fantasy Emmi with real Emmi?<br /><br />What happens then?<br /><br />Many readers have said this, but if you're a fan of David Nicholls's work (particularly One Day, which happens to be one of my all-time favourite reads), then you will love this epistolary novel by Austrian author, Daniel Glattauer.<br /><br />The entire book is written in e-mail format and is a fast-paced, witty and wonderfully relatable novel which was translated to English by Husband and wife duo Jamie Bulloch (Leo's voice) and katharina Bielenberg (Emmi).<br /><br />I must confess I wasn't sure what to expect when I started reading this book, but the easy, relaxed writing style (so reminiscent of what most of us would sound like on e-mail), won me over pretty quickly. <br /><br />Daniel Glattauer has a way with words and writes such fabulously snappy, clever dialogue that you can't help but wish that you were on the receiving end of any one of the e-mail responses conducted throughout the entire novel.<br /><br />There's an immediate rapport between Emmi and Leo, who each, seem to try and outdo each other in the sharp, spunky, quick-witted comeback stakes.<br /><br />That there's a virtual chemistry becomes apparent pretty quickly, but with that online attraction, comes a whole new set of emotional issues, jealousy, insecurities and harsh accusations which stems from the fact that the two of them haven't met face to face. <br /><br />Strangely enough, the roles seem to be reversed and Leo seems to be reluctant to meet, while Emmi, despite the fact that she's happily married (or so claims to be), is dead keen on meeting the face behind the E-mail based persona (Somehow, I've always thought that women are more reluctant to meet their online "friends").<br /><br />I thought that Glattauer was pretty accurate in his portrayal of how easy it is to make assumptions when you're not face to face with someone and adeptly showcases how people become trapped in their own perception of what they think is being said as opposed to what they're reading.<br /><br />He drives home the fact that reading people online is no easy feat and that what people perceive as being real, could be the opposite of what they've initially thought.<br /><br />It's this that makes the characters so interesting.<br /><br />Both are not without their flaws; Emmi especially tends to be abrasive and jealously possessive, while hypocritically enough, often refuses to open up about her family life. In fact, Emmi reminds me a lot of Emma from One Day, who was also not all that likeable.<br /><br />Leo, on the other hand, is often restrained and selfishly persists in holding on the image of the fantasy Emmi that he's carved in his mind.<br /><br />Yet, for all that, there's an inherent likability about both of them; two lost souls, who accidentally discovers what it means to be virtual soul mates. But how that translates itself into real life and whether they actually end up meeting is something you'll have to discover for yourself.<br /><br />What I can say is that you should be prepared for a few unexpected twists and an unexpected ending that leaves room for a sequel, which I believe is already in the works.<br /><br />It's a wonderfully addictive novel which can be read in one sitting, and which I believe will appeal to everyone who has ever tried and succeeded and tried and failed at the online dating game. <br /><br />You may probably end up inevitably feeling like you're invading the intensely private and intimate liaison between two illicit lovers, but don't let that stop you from reading what I consider to be one of the most cleverly written and incredibly romantic (despite the virtual settings) novels of this year so far. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3843257652681477733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_565216461" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402786747" href="/book/show/9745480-love-virtually">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18383778-dolors?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer565216461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1256351153490244964">(Still not published in English, read in Spanish)<br/>After having read the earlier Glattauer's novel I had been anxiously waiting for its sequel.<br/>I got it only yesterday, late in the evening.<br/>I finished it today.<br/>Beware, because once you enter Emmi and Leo's world you'll be completely hooked, you won't be able to put the book down.<br/>This might be seen and even reviewed as a trivial, page-turner, modern epistolary love story. Only another of those fresh-and-easy-reading books to take away with you for a s</span>
  <span id="freeText1256351153490244964" style="display:none">(Still not published in English, read in Spanish)<br />After having read the earlier Glattauer's novel I had been anxiously waiting for its sequel.<br />I got it only yesterday, late in the evening.<br />I finished it today.<br />Beware, because once you enter Emmi and Leo's world you'll be completely hooked, you won't be able to put the book down.<br />This might be seen and even reviewed as a trivial, page-turner, modern epistolary love story. Only another of those fresh-and-easy-reading books to take away with you for a short holiday. Don't be fooled.<br />If you read between the lines, if you bother to look deeper, it can almost reach the level of pure philosophy. This story is about all of us. It COULD be any of us. <br />Emmi and Leo are two lost people who think they are contented with their lives until they "meet virtually" by accident. A silly mistake. The connection begins. Game is on.<br />Only through their mails we witness the full development of an intimate and complex relationship, we spy on two bare souls exposed to each other, their hidden wishes, their fears, their regrets, their dreams are shown to us without restraint. And I felt so identified with so many of their longings (...)<br />I'm still surfing on the seventh wave, in a sea full of illusion, ideals and "it's-not-impossible-to-have-it-alls".<br /><br />Some great quotations from the book:<br /><br />" Each syllable has your eyes in it"<br /><br />"If you are sober, drink.<br />If you feel quiet, speak.<br />If you are bewildered, ask me.<br />That's why you've got your diary"<br /><br />" Why I never let go of you? Because I can't lose and I don't want to. Because I don't want to lose you".<br /><br />" There's some who live the lack of wind as an inner peace. There's some who live it as a perpetual paralysis".<br /><br />"Until now, only with words, we have reached everywhere".<br /><br />"Write to me, Emmi. Writing is like kissing, but without lips. Writing is giving kisses of thoughts".<br /><br />A sequel that didn't deceive. Don't miss it.<br />I still believe in magic !!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1256351153490244964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2923528383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15703380884644253289">This felt a bit like watching old people flirt, tbh. Not sure if it was because I read this in German, or the fact that they didn’t switch to a first name basis until the very end but the prose felt quite formal, sometimes stuffy, often very flowery and therefore, old. <br/>Both characters were very eloquent, particularly Emmi. She was quirky and funny, sarcastic, with a very sharp tongue and the story just flew along and was very easy to read, despite what I said earlier about the prose. This, plus </span>
  <span id="freeText15703380884644253289" style="display:none">This felt a bit like watching old people flirt, tbh. Not sure if it was because I read this in German, or the fact that they didn’t switch to a first name basis until the very end but the prose felt quite formal, sometimes stuffy, often very flowery and therefore, old. <br />Both characters were very eloquent, particularly Emmi. She was quirky and funny, sarcastic, with a very sharp tongue and the story just flew along and was very easy to read, despite what I said earlier about the prose. This, plus the immense curiosity to see how everything turned out (will they meet or won’t they?!) really made this an incredibly quick read. I stayed up way too late to finish this. However, I have yet to decide whether or not I’m going to pick up the sequel. I’m not sure if this can work a second time.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer157317493" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4059904640544281206">So this book is a bit like vox for the net millennium. I have a weird relationship to this book. <br/><br/>basically the guy that I currently have a "relationship" with is a guy I've known for 6 years online. we hung out years ago in the same forum. I know people in real life that have met him in real life. we both know people online that have met the other in real life. he's been to new york, for all we know in the same room as me. basically the internet is a very complicated network of people who intera</span>
  <span id="freeText4059904640544281206" style="display:none">So this book is a bit like vox for the net millennium. I have a weird relationship to this book. <br /><br />basically the guy that I currently have a "relationship" with is a guy I've known for 6 years online. we hung out years ago in the same forum. I know people in real life that have met him in real life. we both know people online that have met the other in real life. he's been to new york, for all we know in the same room as me. basically the internet is a very complicated network of people who interact on all different kinds of levels. I have to say as part of the tech savvy youth, I am commonly texting, emailing and iming within a group of 3 or 4 people, most of whom are using more than one method of communication.<br /><br />for example currently. David: text, im, forum. Dave: im, forum. Pix: im. Kennedy: forum. you're getting the picture. basically tech interaction in surround sound. <br /><br />On the other hand I think I've made it abundantly clear that I am a huge fan of the epistolary novel. so bringing these things together works for me. <br /><br />I don't know on the other hand if these things coming together would work for people who aren't really part of that world. I mean I think my mom would just be confused how they even met online. I mean a mistaken email... (this happens in matt beaumont too! it's a theme). I think this novel is a very direct thing that you have to understand from a specific view of the world. <br /><br />basically I'm just standing in the exact right position to enjoy this novel. Plus I love language psychology. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and I am so fucking glad they didn't meet. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer294133100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer402062210726122439">Translated from the German by Katherina Bielenberg and Jamie Bulloch.<br/><br/>Opening:<br/><br/><b><i>15 January</i><br/><br/><u>SUBJECT. CANCELLING MY SUBSCRIPTION</u><br/><br/>I would like to cancel my subscription. Can I do so by e-mail?<br/><br/>Best wishes<br/>E. Rother</b><br/><br/>Original title Gut gegen Nordwind should have been kept even though the body was translated into English. <br/><br/>Unputdownable.<br/><br/><br/><br/></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9782253157304" href="/book/show/10784505-quand-souffle-le-vent-du-nord">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71147186-justine?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71147186-justine?shelf=romance">romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2127791710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3068325310820715266">I thought I wouldn't really like this book, as it's clearly a romance, and I don't really love this genre. But <i>Love Virtually</i> was in my TBR; it's been a long time and I decided to read some of the oldest books there! So I gave it a chance.<br/><br/>I didn't know it was epistolary. And I love this kind of novel! Moreover, it was well written, even if it was translated! <br/><br/>Then, the characters. Both Leo and Emmi are either super annoying, or super endearing! They can be sarcastic, ironic, mean, vengeful; but a</span>
  <span id="freeText3068325310820715266" style="display:none">I thought I wouldn't really like this book, as it's clearly a romance, and I don't really love this genre. But <i>Love Virtually</i> was in my TBR; it's been a long time and I decided to read some of the oldest books there! So I gave it a chance.<br /><br />I didn't know it was epistolary. And I love this kind of novel! Moreover, it was well written, even if it was translated! <br /><br />Then, the characters. Both Leo and Emmi are either super annoying, or super endearing! They can be sarcastic, ironic, mean, vengeful; but also cheesy, sensual, loving, desperate. The reader witnesses the evolution of their feelings, and it was really well made. Big clichés are put forward just to be dismantled. <br /><br />Only problem: it becomes repetitive at some point, before the novel takes a different direction. And the dates are not mentioned; there's only "Three minutes later", "Two days later", so it's quite hard to visualize the chronology. <br /><br />The ending though! I realized I loved the novel when it abruptly ended and I wanted more!! So, I'll go get the second book as soon as possible! </span>
  <a data-text-id="3068325310820715266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer236912647" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3051306945033158910">The Short of It<br/><br/>Realistic portrayal of an online affair.<br/><br/>The Long of It<br/><br/>Emmi Rothner accidently e-mails Leo Leike. No seriously. She does. She’s trying to cancel a magazine order and accidently hits an extra period or delete a letter, whatever. Haha mistake happened and both parties involved laugh a little (LOL anyone?) and life went on.<br/><br/>Until it happened again. This time Emmi is a wee bit more irate at magazine company and Leo comes back equally as snarky. Hahaha giggles ensue AGAIN. And the next t</span>
  <span id="freeText3051306945033158910" style="display:none">The Short of It<br /><br />Realistic portrayal of an online affair.<br /><br />The Long of It<br /><br />Emmi Rothner accidently e-mails Leo Leike. No seriously. She does. She’s trying to cancel a magazine order and accidently hits an extra period or delete a letter, whatever. Haha mistake happened and both parties involved laugh a little (LOL anyone?) and life went on.<br /><br />Until it happened again. This time Emmi is a wee bit more irate at magazine company and Leo comes back equally as snarky. Hahaha giggles ensue AGAIN. And the next thing you know a correspondence begins.<br /><br />Thus, we enter the world of courtship via the interwebs. The emails begin humorously, a bit of snark here and-a-bit-a sentiment there. All in good fun.<br /><br />But, just like any long-term virtual correspondence, errors are gonna be made, miscommunications are gonna happen, and feelings are gonna get hurt.<br /><br />Do Emmi and Leo make a love connection? Or is it nothing more than a virtual farce?<br /><br />The Thoughts about It<br /><br />Hahaha I don’t thnk that I often leave my reviews with rhetorical questions but I just can’t help it with this one. Let me tell you what, the cover made me all SKETCHY. I mean, check it out, folks. So AmericanLove, yes? (I much prefer the European cover)<br /><br /> Man, those Germans know how to pull you in and make your heart do summersaults until you feel like your rightside up only to be laying flat-faced to the ground trying to breath.<br /><br />Yeah, I sorta dug this book, heh. Seriously. It is Realistic. In that jab-your-eye-out realism of meeting someone and kinda wanting to get your hopes up that it’ll Last and be Real and Forever but still holding your heart back because you don’t want it Broken and Sobbing.<br /><br />Can I make up an award? Most Believable Love Story in the Twenty-First Centruy.</span>

<div id="review_284812554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/284812554" />
    <a title="Boorrito" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3587328-boorrito"><img alt="Boorrito" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393624280p2/3587328.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284812554?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Boorrito" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Boorrito" href="/user/show/3587328-boorrito">Boorrito</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781906694975" href="/book/show/8928842-love-virtually">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3587328-boorrito?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3587328-boorrito?shelf=germany">germany</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284812554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9083012200703134842">This is one of those books where the context of when I read it is probably super important. If I had read it a week ago I probably wouldn't have enjoyed it so much.<br/>Since I read it today, when I was freeeee and not totally stressed out I did enjoy it and finished it in a few hours instead. <br/><br/>The "emails between two characters" narrative device could have been so, so annoying. But it wasn't because they read like actual emails a real person would send (apart from having better spelling), making it f</span>
  <span id="freeText9083012200703134842" style="display:none">This is one of those books where the context of when I read it is probably super important. If I had read it a week ago I probably wouldn't have enjoyed it so much.<br />Since I read it today, when I was freeeee and not totally stressed out I did enjoy it and finished it in a few hours instead. <br /><br />The "emails between two characters" narrative device could have been so, so annoying. But it wasn't because they read like actual emails a real person would send (apart from having better spelling), making it feel less contrived! And having recently heard of a true-life story of two people falling in love due to someone making a mistake in an email address it didn't seem cutesy that it happened here. <br /><br />The translation was also very good. It didn't read like it was translated which is probably the best compliment you can give to a translation. This might be partly because German isn't as awkward to translate into readable English as Russian and Japanese, the two languages which most of the translations I've been reading lately come from. However they still could have ballesed it up so good on them!<br /><br />I think the translation is also good partly because there's nothing, well, super "German" about this book beyond the fact that it's set there. You could have changed the setting to somewhere else and it wouldn't have affected the story greatly. You can choose yourself if this is a sad indictment of globalisation or a sign of the universal nature of falling in love (via email). (Personally I choose the latter.)<br /><br />In conclusion, interesting book, cliffhanger ending that does make me want to read the sequel instead of pissing me off (that's a tough thing to pull off) and good translation. If it sounds like something you'd like, give a shot! </span>
  <a data-text-id="9083012200703134842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3200319641" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3200319641" />
    <a title="Ioana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19636467-ioana"><img alt="Ioana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366554859p2/19636467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3200319641?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ioana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ioana" href="/user/show/19636467-ioana">Ioana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857050953" href="/book/show/12640615-love-virtually">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3200319641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9737936207423301197">Told entirely through email, this book reads like a romcom featuring Emmi and Leo, who meet by chance online, when Emmi unintentionally emails Leo instead of the magazine she wanted to unsubscribe from.<br/><br/>Their exchange is playful, witty and creative, and I can definitely see people reading this in one go because it's very dynamic, captivating, and there is a lot of back and forth and flow that stands as evidence to the chemistry between the characters. It truly is a charming book, even if it might</span>
  <span id="freeText9737936207423301197" style="display:none">Told entirely through email, this book reads like a romcom featuring Emmi and Leo, who meet by chance online, when Emmi unintentionally emails Leo instead of the magazine she wanted to unsubscribe from.<br /><br />Their exchange is playful, witty and creative, and I can definitely see people reading this in one go because it's very dynamic, captivating, and there is a lot of back and forth and flow that stands as evidence to the chemistry between the characters. It truly is a charming book, even if it might seem like something not very special. <br /><br />The characters are imperfect, yet both really likeable and especially relatable. Emmi is capricious, flirty and demands non-stop attention. She has a desire for adventure and a desire for appreciation. Leo is melancholic, calm and incredibly intelligent. Their exchange often relied on analyses of previous things they've written and goes from playful to provocative to romantic. It's an emotional whirlwind where it's impossible that you won't feel at least a bit for the characters! I also found Bernhard's (keeping it spoiler-free!) emails to be heart-felt and also enjoyed his introduction as an active party, that added a lot to the story and grounded it into what it means for the main character's 'real' lives.<br /><br />I could have seen the ending go either way, and I am honestly happy it went the way it did, though I could see some readers being frustrated about it. Can't wait to read book two!<br /><br />Quick note: I read this book in the original German (but I like keeping my reading list in English for consistency) and the title would actually be 'Good against the North Wind' which makes so much more sense!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9737936207423301197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_574809236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/574809236" />
    <a title="Tusam D.Clide" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18382173-tusam-d-clide"><img alt="Tusam D.Clide" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364473479p2/18382173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/574809236?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tusam D.Clide" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tusam D.Clide" href="/user/show/18382173-tusam-d-clide">Tusam D.Clide</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402786747" href="/book/show/9745480-love-virtually">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer574809236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15932757891794849509">No spoiler here. <br/><br/>At first the purpose of picking up the book was to be entertained. Two people, opposite sex, start trading e-mails randomly then soon falling for each other? One heck of cliche right there. The weariness of my head had severed after reading philosophical tributes to significant matters of life by famous thinkers. I wanted to a breeze, and the title (Gut Gegen Nordwind : Good Against North Wind - I honestly think it is stupid to call the book ' Love Virtually ' ) fitted what I lo</span>
  <span id="freeText15932757891794849509" style="display:none">No spoiler here. <br /><br />At first the purpose of picking up the book was to be entertained. Two people, opposite sex, start trading e-mails randomly then soon falling for each other? One heck of cliche right there. The weariness of my head had severed after reading philosophical tributes to significant matters of life by famous thinkers. I wanted to a breeze, and the title (Gut Gegen Nordwind : Good Against North Wind - I honestly think it is stupid to call the book ' Love Virtually ' ) fitted what I longed for as well. <br /><br />The first quarter gave me what I wanted, fun, quick-paced, no head-breaking drama and most of all- entertaining breeze. Through Leo and Emmi comfortable tempo was created - and getting thicker as their getting-to-know phase broadened each other's perception of humane aspect. See, the book utilized what was expected from the readers tremendously well. It implanted a sense of love growing, at the right tempo with the right push/pull. <br /><br />What is so brilliant about the book comes after the first half. The story develops to the question that was bound to occur 'Will it work?' - The writer keeps on bringing the question to the surface where the reader is too consumed in the story to neglect. It is amazing how the mysterious nature of male-female chemistry sweetens AND sours the story. (the mixed pattern is insanely delicious)<br /><br />No spoiler here. In the end the book is about two people forming a virtual love in which freedom from the real world's limited affiliations exist. As one could expect you will not let go of the book due to the curiosity regarding whether these two characters will end up loving in real life. Though a cliche structure, the way the story flows - the way each character is shown and hidden - the ambiguity but also the clarity ! of the book is, as I said, brilliant. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15932757891794849509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402786747" href="/book/show/9745480-love-virtually">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3208977521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15969777984576894413">I picked up this book as a joke. I found a copy of it lying in a second-hand bookstore. The back cover had a cheesy dialogue that I found funny and so I decided to read it. I had no idea what I was in for. But more surprisingly, I never thought I'd actually like the book. <br/><br/>The premise is a simple one. A woman writes an email to unsubscribe from a magazine. She gets a reply from a man who informs her that she has the wrong e-mail ID, and thus begins their story. The entire novel is epistolary. The</span>
  <span id="freeText15969777984576894413" style="display:none">I picked up this book as a joke. I found a copy of it lying in a second-hand bookstore. The back cover had a cheesy dialogue that I found funny and so I decided to read it. I had no idea what I was in for. But more surprisingly, I never thought I'd actually like the book. <br /><br />The premise is a simple one. A woman writes an email to unsubscribe from a magazine. She gets a reply from a man who informs her that she has the wrong e-mail ID, and thus begins their story. The entire novel is epistolary. The reader follows the story through the email correspondence between the two main characters. <br /><br />It's actually a little difficult to introduce other characters, subplots and elements which affect the relationship between two people who are only corresponding by email. And I think that was done well by the author. <br /><br />I finished the book in a little more than a day. I was hooked to it. Maybe because it's such an easy read. Or maybe because I understood the angst that comes with the ambiguity of such a relationship? The two haven't seen each other or met. But they still correspond, even if it's about the most mundane parts of their day. However, it's that notification in their inboxes that matters the most. <br /><br />The characters have their flaws. You can feel it through every typed word. Perhaps that's why I enjoyed reading it. I can see why the book can be disliked given its over-sensitive characters and typical rom-com tropes. I won't deny my bias here. I read it when I was in the mood for something like that. I'd recommend it to anyone who wants to get out of a book slump. Maybe the book will become your guilty pleasure. <br /><br />P. S. The novel has been adapted into a radio drama by BBC Radio 4. If you can't read the book, have a listen to David Tennant read the e-mails!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15969777984576894413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_676207373" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/676207373" />
    <a title="Veri K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22489183-veri-k"><img alt="Veri K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515432331p2/22489183.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/676207373?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veri K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veri K" href="/user/show/22489183-veri-k">Veri K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer676207373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7912868567053879106">I have to admit, the first time I read the book I did NOT like it! I thought that the protagonists never got to the point, I skimmed many parts and didn't read them carefully enough because I just wanted to know how the story will end. Big mistake.<br/>Neither did I like one of the protagonists, Emmi. I thought she was annoying and absolutely impudent (she still is, in some ways). To me she was dislikable in every way. Her attitude was also one of the factors why I didnt enjoy reading it.<br/><br/><br/>But when I r</span>
  <span id="freeText7912868567053879106" style="display:none">I have to admit, the first time I read the book I did NOT like it! I thought that the protagonists never got to the point, I skimmed many parts and didn't read them carefully enough because I just wanted to know how the story will end. Big mistake.<br />Neither did I like one of the protagonists, Emmi. I thought she was annoying and absolutely impudent (she still is, in some ways). To me she was dislikable in every way. Her attitude was also one of the factors why I didnt enjoy reading it.<br /><br /><br />But when I read it a second and a third and I think even a forth time I got to love it. The main characters write in such a beautiful language, with so many details, which got deep under my skin. (Here I have to add that I read it in German, and I don't know if the book in English is as good) For me it didn't matter anymore what they said and if they will meet and what course of action will happen next, but HOW they expressed themselves and their feelings. I know passages by heart, I could read it all over again. <br /><br />As for the characters themselves, their language defines which person they are. It's the only clue the reader gets to know them. Also the difference between writing something and actually talking and acting (and being somebody) is adressed, which makes the two characters real, even though they are playing a role by writing mails.<br /><br />For somebody who didn't like the book I'd advise him/her to re-read it. Maybe that will give you the time not to focus on the story itself anymore, but on the amazing language in which the two protagonist express themselves. And maybe you get to love it like I do now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7912868567053879106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18033354643247324340"><i>From BBC Radio 4 - Afternoon Drama:<br/>Starring David Tennant and Emilia Fox, Love Virtually by Austrian novelist Daniel Glattauer is a thoroughly modern epistolary novel with one difference - its protagonists Emmi Rothner and Leo Leike communicate exclusively by email.<br/><br/>The European answer to You've got Mail.<br/><br/>Two million copies sold in Germany to date. And bought by thirty-five publishers around the world, Love Virtually by Austrian novelist Daniel Glattauer, is well on the way to becoming a global pu</i></span>
  <span id="freeText18033354643247324340" style="display:none"><i>From BBC Radio 4 - Afternoon Drama:<br />Starring David Tennant and Emilia Fox, Love Virtually by Austrian novelist Daniel Glattauer is a thoroughly modern epistolary novel with one difference - its protagonists Emmi Rothner and Leo Leike communicate exclusively by email.<br /><br />The European answer to You've got Mail.<br /><br />Two million copies sold in Germany to date. And bought by thirty-five publishers around the world, Love Virtually by Austrian novelist Daniel Glattauer, is well on the way to becoming a global publishing phenomenon.<br /><br />They "meet" when Emmi mistakenly sends an e-mail to Leo's inbox. A romance ensues that allows them to live out a shared secret life far removed from their day-to-day existences. But to what extent does it rely on fantasy and escapism, and will it survive a real-life meeting?<br /><br />The problem is...Emmi (a modern Madame Bovary) is married....<br /><br />Have email, Facebook, texting and the like created a generation of isolated young people who prefer to communicate remotely - who may be in fact afraid to engage in face to face contact to find love? Is it possible to fall in love with someone you've never met? Does a virtual affair 'count' as adultery? What are the implications of the fact that we can pretend to be anyone in cyberspace?<br /><br />Adapted by Eileen Horne.<br /><br />Produced by Clive Brill</i></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dr4NwVcICiIHzX7iRPgcQOc3kH+ZXxtrEDk+zaTMs7RQyaq8uupF3+BbN9PK3S06e3kYwSK6MOCTWtcu78D+wQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VswD5IkcGB4yeDRy62nBhy8r8UB68C5QxyoXlaIpBfpwu6SZZP5X49XufUNlTPD9s2V5/sEVBdtESf526SVIjw==')})

Karo mit ihrem mittelmäßigen Freund, den sie verlässt. Karo heulend am Telefon, um ihren Freund, den sie nicht will, (erfolglos) zurückzubekommen. Aber auch Kuttners Roman hat Schwächen, und die haben eben mit der psychologischen Ausgestaltung der Hauptfigur zu tun. Denn Karo ist zwar sympathisch und chaotisch, aber sie hat nicht das mindeste Geheimnis mehr. Alles über ihr Wesen wird in der Ich-Perspektive durch Selbstreflexionen aufgeschlüsselt, nichts entwickelt sich aus der Geschichte selbst. So will man als Psychiater im offenen Buch einer Patientin lesen. Aber von einem Roman erwartet man als Leser schon ein bisschen mehr.\n\nVielleicht ist dieses &quot;mehr&quot; aber gar nicht so wichtig. Denn Karo ist eine kluge, witzige, beizeiten auch selbstironische junge Frau, und Kuttner ist eine mindestens ebenso kluge und witzige wie genaue Beobachterin der kleinen Schwächen postmoderner Menschen um die Dreißig. Das findet sich auch im Duktus von Mängelexemplar wieder – etwa da, wo er die anglizismisierte Computersprache (gedownloaded) in die Beschreibung eines Abendessens (&quot;geabendbrotet&quot;) transformiert. So sollte man Mängelexemplar trotz aller Mängel trotzdem lesen. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer794473463559615591">Daniel Glattauer, geboren 1960 in Wien, studierte Pädagogik (Diplomarbeit “Das Böse in der Erziehung”). Zunächst Hobby-Literat, -Liedermacher und Kellner, später Journalist, zuerst Redakteur bei der Presse, dann zwanzig Jahre Autor bei der österreichischen Tageszeitung „Der Standard“. Zwischendurch und jetzt erst recht: Schriftsteller. Verheiratet, ein großes Kind, leider keinen Hund mehr, dafür f</span>
  <span id="freeText794473463559615591" style="display:none">Daniel Glattauer, geboren 1960 in Wien, studierte Pädagogik (Diplomarbeit “Das Böse in der Erziehung”). Zunächst Hobby-Literat, -Liedermacher und Kellner, später Journalist, zuerst Redakteur bei der Presse, dann zwanzig Jahre Autor bei der österreichischen Tageszeitung „Der Standard“. Zwischendurch und jetzt erst recht: Schriftsteller. Verheiratet, ein großes Kind, leider keinen Hund mehr, dafür fünf indische Laufenten im Landhaus im niederösterreichischen Waldviertel.<br /><br />Bücher (u.a.): „Die Ameisenzählung“ (2001), „Darum“ (2003), „Die Vögel brüllen“ (2004), „Der Weihnachtshund“ (Neuausgabe 2004), „Schauma mal” (2009), „Theo. Antworten aus dem Kinderzimmer (2010)”, „Ewig Dein” (2012) und „Die Wunderübung” (2014).<br /><br />Mit seinen beiden Romanen „Gut gegen Nordwind“ (2006) und „Alle sieben Wellen“ (2009) gelangen ihm zwei Bestseller, die in zahlreiche Sprachen übersetzt und auch als Hörspiel, Theaterstück und Hörbuch zum Erfolg wurden. „Mama, jetzt nicht!“ (2011) ist ein Band mit Kolumnen aus dem Alltag, die über viele Jahre im „Standard“ erschienen sind.<br /><br />2006 Nominierung Deutscher Buchpreis</span>
  <a data-text-id="794473463559615591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
